Local News

Coup in Fujian Province Becomes a Reality; People's Government Appears Yesterday; Li Jishen as Chairman, or Possibly Hu Hanmin; Chen Cai and Chen Youren, etc., Appointed to Key Positions; Fuzhou Central Bank Has Been Sealed Off; Transportation Normal Except for Telegrams

Xin Sheng News Agency reports: The coup in Fujian Province has been fluctuating in recent days, but ultimately, Li Jishen and Chen Mingshu, in their final political struggle, have taken a desperate gamble. Yesterday morning, the Fujian Provincial People's Congress finally passed the political program and list of candidates for the independent government. The various news items are recorded below:

Political Organization

The Chairman of the People's Government is Li Jishen. Underneath are five committee members: (1) Chairman of the Political Committee: Chen Mingshu, (2) Chairman of the Military Committee: Cai Tingkai, (3) Chairman of the Finance Committee: Xu Chongqing, (4) Chairman of the Education Committee: Zhang Bojun, (5) Chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee: Chen Youren. According to the composition of the above people, the factions are quite complex.

The So-Called Political Program

The so-called Provisional National People's Congress was held in Fuzhou yesterday morning. A preparatory office had been set up in advance, and the Fujian Provincial Government was instructed in the name of the preparatory office to notify its subordinates to participate. The meeting was ostensibly composed of agriculture, industry, commerce, school, military and government, without a party name. It was resolved to issue a declaration of the rights of the people, advocating the abolition of unequal treaties, the realization of tariff autonomy first, the people's absolute freedom of assembly, publication, strikes, and belief, equal protection of physical and mental labor, distribution of land based on population, and nationalization of forests and mines.

Various Factions Active

The Social Democratic Party, the Third Party, and the Trotskyist-Chen faction are the main driving forces behind the scenes. Young literary figures such as Hu Qiuyuan, who were originally engaged in writing at the Shenzhou Guoguang Society in Shanghai, have now become Chen Mingshu's advisors. Huang Qixiang, Zhang Bojun, and other Third Party leaders are particularly active in the dark.

Financial News

Yesterday morning, foreign sources in this city reported that the Xiamen branch of the Central Bank has been sealed off by the Fujian authorities, and remittances are no longer possible. The market in Fujian Province is in chaos. The Fuzhou County Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday, asking whether Central Bank exchange coupons are still used normally in Shanghai, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang. The City Chamber of Commerce immediately telegraphed back that the coupons are still used normally.

Transportation Situation

When the reporter obtained the accurate news of the coup in Fujian Province, he immediately inquired with various transportation agencies about the current status of transportation between Shanghai and Fujian. According to Hua Shijian, the business manager of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, the Fuzhou telegraph line, south of Jiangshan County in Zhejiang Province, was broken due to the blasting of mountains for road construction since the evening of the 19th, and is not related to the Fujian coup. Repairs are currently underway, and it is expected that normal reporting will be possible tomorrow (i.e., today). As for the ships traveling the Shanghai-Fuzhou route, they are the Taishun of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the Jiesheng of the EWO, the Wanxiang of the Sanbei, and the Huaan of the Changan. The Wanxiang of the Sanbei left Shanghai for Fuzhou as usual at 6 PM last night. The Jiesheng of the EWO is scheduled to sail to Fuzhou today. In addition, the postal service was still normal yesterday.

Private Telegram

Xin Xin News Agency reports: Regarding the brewing of the coup in Fujian Province, the situation became tense again yesterday. According to a private telegram received by a certain Fujian native in Shanghai yesterday (the 20th), the Fuzhou Municipal People's Congress yesterday passed the following list of candidates for the People's Government: Chairman: Hu Hanmin, Vice Chairman: Li Jishen, Chairman of the Military Committee: Cai Tingkai, Commander-in-Chief: Chen Mingshu, Chairman of Finance: Xu Chongqing, Chairman of Foreign Affairs: Chen Youren, Chairman of Education: Zhang Bojun. The policies are: (1) Resistance to Japan, (2) Suppression of Communists, (3) Land Revolution. It is heard that Hu Hanmin is still in Hong Kong and has not yet gone to Fujian.

Source News

Ri Ri News Agency reports: According to a certain source, the Fujian Provincial Government did convene a people's representative conference yesterday, attended by more than one hundred people. They passed the organization of the "Revolutionary Government of the Chinese National Alliance" and decided on the political program and list of candidates. The content of the political program roughly advocates tariff autonomy, the abolition of unequal treaties, the people's right to strike and freedom of belief, and the nationalization of all land, forests, and mines. It also aims to resist Japan, but cancels the slogan of suppressing bandits, which has attracted much attention. In addition, the "Revolutionary United Army of the Chinese National Alliance" was formed, abolishing the Blue Sky White Sun flag, establishing the Production Party on the basis of the Third Party and the Social Democratic Party, and creating another flag. Hu Hanmin has not yet arrived in Fujian, so Li Jishen is acting as the chairman.

Central Attitude

Ri Ri News Agency reports: Since the Fujian coup occurred, the atmosphere has once become calm. For the sake of appeasement, the Central Government initially adopted a wait-and-see attitude, hoping for the Fujian Provincial Authorities' awakening. Unexpectedly, it suddenly became tense again in a few days. Yesterday, a certain naval commander in this city told a Ri Ri News Agency reporter that after President Wang returned to Beijing, he decided to resolve the Fujian affair politically. If necessary, he would send personnel to Fujian to persuade and cancel the plan. Therefore, there was a proposal for Chen Zhaoying and Duan Xipeng to go to Fujian. President Wang believes that the time is appropriate and summoned Chen Jiliang, the commander of the First Naval Fleet, by telegram this morning (i.e., yesterday morning) to immediately go to Beijing to discuss the plan for mediating the Fujian affair. After receiving the order, Chen left Shanghai for Beijing by plane at 1:30 PM today (i.e., yesterday) to meet President Wang. He plans to return to Shanghai tomorrow morning (i.e., this morning). If necessary, Chen may also go to Fujian.

Song Qingling Did Not Go to Fujian

According to a Central News Agency report from Fuzhou, Sun Yat-sen's widow, Madam Song Qingling, had arrived in Fuzhou. Yesterday morning, a Central News Agency reporter visited Madam Sun's residence on Avenue Molière (today's Huaihai Zhong Road), but she was out. Her family members said that Madam Sun was indeed in Shanghai but had gone out on business. The reporter then inquired with Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi at his residence, who replied that the news from Fujian stating that Madam Sun had arrived in Fuzhou was completely inaccurate, as he had spoken with Madam Sun on the phone that very morning. As for the matter of General Cai Tingkai being summoned to Jiangxi by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, he had no knowledge of it.

News from Naval Circles

The Min Yan News Agency reports that since Huang Qiang took office as the Garrison Commander of Zhangzhou and Xiamen, Lin Guogeng, the Commander of the Xiamen Naval Port, has sent numerous lengthy telegrams to the naval authorities, reporting on the situation there. According to claims from the 19th Route Army, the army is responsible for the local administration of Xiamen, while the naval port defense remains under the navy. Currently, a state of peace is being maintained. However, yesterday's political change in Fujian has officially materialized. The Mawei Naval Port Headquarters is close to the provincial capital, and the large-scale Mawei Naval Shipyard is also located there. If, unfortunately, the situation escalates into military action, the defense of Mawei will also be a serious issue between the army and navy. It is reported that the commander of the naval port, Li Mengbin, sends daily telegrams to the naval department.

Chiang Yan's Statement

The Xin Xin News Agency reports that Chiang Yan, the Brigade Commander of the 166th Brigade of the 56th Division stationed in Fujian, resigned from his post in Fujian and came to Shanghai the day before yesterday, staying at the residence of his friend Tao Jianfeng. A Xin Xin News Agency reporter visited him yesterday and inquired about the truth of the Fujian Incident. He issued the following written statement: (1) He had no mission here and, due to his position, did not wish to comment on the Fujian situation to avoid causing misunderstandings; (2) Fujian is currently quite peaceful, but due to rumors, a state of martial law has been lightly imposed. Correspondence, telegrams, and news are being checked. All agencies are operating as usual; (3) Chiang Yan's future actions will depend on orders from his superiors; (4) Although some prominent individuals out of office have gone to Fujian, they are traveling and visiting friends. The rumors are being spread by disgruntled elements; (5) There is no news regarding the rumors that Chiang Yan will be transferred to Jiangxi to suppress bandits or appointed as a councilor to the Military Advisory Council.

General Yang Going to Nanjing

The Xin Xin News Agency reports that Yang Dezhao, the representative in Nanjing of Chen Jitang, the Commander-in-Chief of the Southern Route Bandit Suppression, arrived in Shanghai by ship from Hong Kong the day before yesterday afternoon. It is learned that Yang will depart from Shanghai for Nanjing today (the 21st) to pay his respects to Executive Yuan President Wang Jingwei and report on everything. It is said that after arriving in Nanjing, Yang will travel to Jiangxi to pay his respects to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and present a statement.

Zhang and Lu Arrive in Shanghai

The Min Yan News Agency reports that Zhang Zhen, former Commander of the 49th Division of Fujian and a member of the Central Committee, arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday. Since his removal from military command, he has devoted himself to the party affairs of the Central Government. He does not wish to comment on the current changes in the political situation in Fujian. It is also reported that Lu Xingrong, the Deputy Commander of the newly formed 2nd Division, recently went to Nanjing to visit important figures and report on defense matters. He had become ill due to overwork during the recent bandit suppression campaign, and his condition was aggravated by the long journey. He has returned to Shanghai from Nanjing and has been admitted to a hospital for treatment. His relatives, friends, and subordinates here have been visiting him.

Sun Ke Speaks Painfully About the Fujian Incident: The Country is Facing Many Difficulties and Should Not Be Divided, Liu Weizhi Will Still Go to Jiangxi After Arriving in Shanghai, No News About Chen Youren Going to Fujian

The brewing of the Fujian affair has become a reality. Yesterday morning, reporters from various newspapers visited Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke to inquire about the Fujian Incident and his views on the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia. His remarks are recorded as follows:

The Brewing of the Fujian Incident is Gradually Becoming a Reality

Sun Ke first stated, "Li Jishen has indeed arrived in Fujian. I do not know if Chen Youren has also arrived in Fujian. I have heard that their People's Government will be established in Fuzhou. I also do not know if they have issued a circular telegram. However, I know that the Central Bank in Fujian has been confiscated. The brewing of the Fujian incident is indeed gradually becoming a reality."

The Issue of Welcoming Hu and Others to Nanjing

The reporter then asked about the Central Government welcoming Hu Hanmin, Li Jishen, Chen Mingshu, and Feng Yuxiang to Nanjing. Sun Ke replied, "This matter may have been decided temporarily by President Wang after he returned to Nanjing from Shanghai the day before yesterday. I do not yet know the specifics." Sun Ke also stated that when the Standing Committee of the Economic Committee held a meeting in Shanghai last Saturday, they had discussed the Fujian Incident but only exchanged information and did not conduct a formal discussion.

The Country is Facing Many Difficulties and Should Not Be Divided

Sun Ke continued, "In my personal observation, Mr. Li Jishen, Mr. Chen Youren, and Mr. Chen Zhenru of the 19th Route Army have always been relied upon by the Central Government and have a long history in the party and the country. Reason dictates that they would not take such action. Even if they disagree with the Central Government's policies or have personal disagreements, they should communicate frankly and not involve politics or military matters lightly, which would result in the country being divided when it is already facing many difficulties. This would make it even more difficult to rectify domestic affairs and respond to foreign threats. In my opinion, at this time, we should unite, seek common defense against external enemies, and work together to strengthen the country."

Liu Weizhi Visited Sun Yesterday Morning

He also said, "Vice Minister of Industry Liu Weizhi has already arrived in Shanghai from Jiangxi via Nanjing this morning and has met with me. The discussion was about the Fujian situation. However, Liu's trip to Jiangxi was not on my behalf but was in response to Chiang's summons for a face-to-face discussion." According to Liu, Chairman Chiang and others hope that the Fujian situation will not become a reality. According to reporters, Liu Weizhi will report to various parties in Nanjing and Shanghai and then return to Nanchang next Friday, or the following week if there is not enough time, to report to Chiang.

Observations on the Resumption of Diplomatic Relations Between the United States and Russia

Subsequently, Sun Ke also spoke at length about the issue of the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia. The resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia has already materialized. The obvious reason for the resumption of diplomatic relations is economic relations: the United States wants to obtain foreign markets for its economic recovery plan, while Russia wants to obtain machinery, cotton raw materials, and credit loans. In reality, it is also said that the focus of the resumption of diplomatic relations between the United States and Russia is the Far East issue. The two sides have some kind of military agreement. If, unfortunately, changes occur in the Far East, a union between the United States and Russia is indeed possible. In terms of strength, although Japan's army and navy are currently strong, they are not as strong as the United States and Russia, which is naturally unfavorable to Japan. However, air power is the key to this matter, and it depends on whether there are any changes in the policies of the Japanese military. If Japan still dreams of realizing its continental policy, then unfortunate events are difficult to predict. But no matter who wins or loses, Japan will inevitably occupy North China as a base against Russia and blockade our coastal ports against the United States. Our country will inevitably suffer misfortune and great losses will be difficult to avoid.

Tension in Fujian Causes Guest Merchants to Suspend Trade, and Many Ships Cancel Cargo

Since the Fujian authorities announced martial law, the shipping and trade industries in Shanghai have been affected, with trade suspended and the market disrupted. The details obtained by reporters are recorded as follows:

Suspension of Trade

After the resolution of the dispute between the Sanshan Guild Hall and the National Goods Introduction Office, the Fujian fabric merchants, general merchandise merchants, and grain merchants have been rushing to load large quantities of goods onto the Sanbei, Changan, Yihua, and other ships bound for Fujian. In the past ten days, the ships bound for Fujian have been fully loaded with export goods, and many later arrivals have had to withdraw their customs declarations. The congestion of cargo transportation is rare. Unexpectedly, a sudden change in the Fujian situation occurred, and Fuzhou was suddenly placed under martial law. The news spread, causing unease. Yesterday, the Fuzhou merchants sent an urgent telegram to Shanghai, ordering the Shanghai-based shops to immediately suspend trade. Those who had already prepared their goods were ordered to postpone loading, and those who had not yet been shipped were to temporarily store them in Shanghai warehouses. All Fujian merchants in Shanghai have complied with these orders.

Sharp Reduction in Cargo

Today's Fuzhou liner is the Jardine Matheson's Jie Sheng, a British ship. The ship had been arranged by the Fujian merchants and had an original export cargo of 4,000 tons. The ship was scheduled to load at noon, but because the Fuzhou merchants sent a telegram to suspend trade, each guest merchant temporarily cancelled their tonnage. Yesterday afternoon, the Jie Sheng's cargo for Fujian was only 250 tons, with temporary cancellations accounting for more than 90%. The Shanghai-Fujian shipping routes have also been severely affected, and it is feared that cargo from Fuzhou to Shanghai will also be suspended in the next few days.

Joint Transportation Between China Merchants Bureau and Longhai Railway Implemented Yesterday, Tonghua Ship Returns to Shanghai Today, Longhai Railway Has a Lot of Goods

Joint water and land transportation between the state-owned China Merchants Bureau and the Longhai Railway was implemented yesterday. The Tonghua ship, which was sent by the Bureau to Haizhou to load Longhai Railway's joint transport goods, left Shanghai the day before yesterday morning. Yesterday afternoon, it could reach the railway dock at Laoyao Sunjiashan. The ship was empty when it sailed to Haizhou because there was no cargo to be transported. It was sent specifically to load cargo from various stations on the Longhai Railway to Shanghai, and it is expected to depart today. It is said that the Longhai Railway transports about 200,000 tons of goods to the sea every year, mainly peanuts, cotton, and other local products, while imported foreign goods are only a small amount of daily necessities.

Liu Hongsheng Reports That China Merchants Bureau's Future is Optimistic, Economic Committee Decides to Allocate Huge Sums of Money, Old HSBC Debts to be Paid Off First, Joint Transport is Willing to Cooperate with Civil Aviation

The China Merchants Bureau urgently needs to deal with maturing foreign debts, so it has submitted a request to the Central Government to allocate 15 million yuan first to meet the emergency. Also, signing a joint water and land transportation agreement with the Ministry of Railways has aroused opposition from private companies, accusing the China Merchants Bureau of monopolizing shipping operations. Yesterday, the Bureau held a commemorative week, and General Manager Liu Hongsheng personally attended and reported that a huge sum of 15 million yuan has been raised. He also detailed the addition of new ships, the repair of various wharves, and the implementation of joint transportation, and expressed willingness to cooperate with civil aviation to jointly deal with foreign ships that infringe on our shipping rights. The details are very important, and a summary is given below:

Total Debt

Yesterday, the Bureau's commemorative week was announced the day before by Liu Hongsheng to the General Affairs Section, conveying to all employees in the Bureau that they should gather at the Bureau on Monday morning to listen to General Manager Liu Hongsheng's report on important recent matters within the Bureau. Therefore, all employees arrived early yesterday morning. After Liu arrived at the auditorium and held the usual ceremony, Liu announced that there were three major items to report today: raising money to repay debts, building new ships, repairing docks, and handling joint transportation. Liu said that the China Merchants Bureau's various foreign debts, including interest, amount to about 22 million yuan to date, and all debts have matured. In fact, it is very difficult to delay any longer and must be raised and repaid in a short period of time. This is indeed the biggest problem facing the Bureau.

Huge Sum Raised

The Bureau's operations this year, whether in the Yangtze River or near-sea transportation, have improved compared to the past few years, and the income of each shipping route has also increased. In this situation, the future of operations is very promising, which is also gratifying. However, the most important thing is the foreign debt, and the most urgent thing to repay first is the 10 million yuan from HSBC. The Bureau has already submitted a request to the Ministry, asking the Central Government to allocate 15 million yuan of the Bureau's fund first. The case has been approved by the Central Government and handed over to the Economic Committee for allocation. The Committee raised this case for discussion at a meeting in Shanghai the day before yesterday and approved it, granting the Bureau 15 million yuan as a fund in a short period of time. Any difficult problem can be solved once the fund is received.

Using Gengkuan Funds

The Bureau currently has more than 20 ships, most of which are old and not suitable for current navigation. Therefore, if we want to develop the shipping industry, we must first add new ships to meet the needs of each route. The Bureau has borrowed from the British Boxer Indemnity Fund to build seven new river and sea ships, which have already begun. They can be put into service by the summer and autumn of next year. With the addition of these seven new ships, operations can be developed. We will continue to plan to add more ships in the future. However, the Bureau's docks occupy the most advantageous position in Shanghai, but they have been damaged for many years and must be thoroughly repaired. We are now planning in a comprehensive way, and as soon as the Economic Committee's 15 million yuan is allocated, we can start construction.

Civil Aviation Cooperation

The Bureau's signing of a national water and land joint transportation contract with the Ministry of Railways this time, with the Longhai Railway being the first to be implemented, has been criticized by outsiders who are unaware of the situation, saying that the Bureau is monopolizing transportation, causing misunderstandings among civil aviation companies. In fact, the Bureau's fundamental truth in creating joint transportation lies in resisting foreign ships that infringe on our shipping rights. The Bureau's position is absolutely consistent with the idea of uniting with and cooperating with our national private shipping companies. There is absolutely no intention of having the China Merchants Bureau monopolize the business of each route. For example, the transportation business in the Qinghai line is mostly taken away by a certain country's ships. Without the Bureau's joint transportation, how can it be recovered? Therefore, we sincerely hope that the private shipping companies will understand the Bureau's truth, eliminate anger, and quickly cooperate. The China Merchants Bureau is very willing to sincerely negotiate in order to recover lost shipping rights, which is not only beneficial to the country but also an honor for the shipping merchants.

Famous French Aviator Arrives in Shanghai

The North China Daily News reports that the famous French aviator de Scheppele has been flying for nearly 18 years without ever experiencing an accident. He is coming to China from Europe and will arrive in Shanghai today (the 20th) or tomorrow (the 21st). De Scheppele is flying a Havilland Dragon Rapide, which is the same model as the one flown by the British aviator Mr. and Mrs. Mollison. Its cruising speed is 108 miles per hour, and its maximum speed is 130 miles per hour. It uses two Gipsy Major engines, each with 130 horsepower, mounted on the lower wing, with air-cooled engines on both sides of the fuselage. It has had several long-distance flights and has excellent performance and is particularly fuel-efficient. The plane has two fuel tanks, each with 30 gallons, and can travel 550 miles in no wind. De Scheppele flew to Beiping in April last year and flew over Shanghai. De Scheppele is a lover of flying and said at the time that he had not been on a train for seven years. His wife is also a famous aviator. The two flew around the world in 1928 and then flew to Abyssinia in Africa. They then flew back and forth between Paris and Beijing, back and forth between Paris and Niger, and a trip to South Africa. This time, they flew from Europe to the Far East and are flying from Hong Kong to Shanghai.

The Xin Xin News Agency reports that Count Cippenberk Vicomp Be Siboun, a famous French aviator, has set off from France to Japan on a long-distance flight in a De Havilland Dragon aircraft. He has already arrived in Hong Kong. Xin Xin News Agency reporters learned from the French Consulate yesterday morning that Count Cippenberk will depart from Hong Kong tomorrow morning and is expected to arrive in Shanghai in the afternoon. After arriving in Shanghai, he will stay for two or three days and then fly to Japan, possibly passing through Beiping and Seoul. According to reports, Mr. Cippenberk flew from Paris, the capital of France, to Beiping in April last year and passed through Shanghai once.

Shanghai Money Shops Subscribed to the Ministry of Finance's New Loan and Paid to the Joint Reserve Treasury Yesterday, Total Amount Received Has Reached More Than 970,000 Yuan, The Deficit Will Be Covered by the Reserve Treasury

The Dagong News Agency reports that Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi urgently needed military expenses for bandit suppression, so he mortgaged 5 million yuan of the 22-year customs treasury bills to Shanghai money shops for a cash loan of 2.5 million yuan. The Shanghai Money Shops Association held an extraordinary general meeting on the 16th of this month and resolved to subscribe to 1 million yuan, with each money shop subscribing to 15,000 yuan. Yesterday (the 20th), all money shops paid the money in full. The Money Shops Joint Reserve Treasury can distribute and send the treasury bills once they are received. Yesterday's report on Qin Runqing's remarks was completely untrue. The Shanghai Money Shops Association was deeply surprised. The information obtained by the Dagong News Agency reporter from the Shanghai Money Shops Association yesterday is recorded as follows:

Loan Facts

A reporter from the Ta Kung Pao newspaper made a special trip yesterday morning to the Shanghai Money Trade Association to inquire about the truth of the Ministry of Finance's loan incident. According to the person in charge of the Association, the Ministry of Finance used twenty-second year customs treasury bonds with a face value of 5 million yuan to borrow 2.5 million yuan in cash from the industry. The Association convened a special meeting of member representatives on the 16th of this month and decided to borrow 1 million yuan. The method was that each member money shop would borrow 15,000 yuan. However, members with insufficient financial resources or smaller scale could reduce the amount as appropriate. The shortfall would be covered by the money industry reserve. A notice was issued by the Association on the 17th of this month, requiring all money shops to pay the money by the 20th of this month (yesterday). However, today's newspapers carried a news report from a certain news agency, saying that Qin Runqing denied the loan, which is very surprising. The news reported by the agency is not the truth. Mr. Qin Runqing, as the chairman of the Association, would never make such a statement. Otherwise, the reporter must have misunderstood. The fact that the Ministry of Finance has established a new loan of 1 million yuan with the money industry is indeed true. As for the previous loan, it has already passed. The two matters are completely different and cannot be confused, and so on.

Association Notice

The Money Trade Association issued a notice on the 17th of this month, which reads: Respectfully inform you that the Ministry of Finance has instructed that 22nd year customs treasury bonds with a face value of 5 million yuan will be used to borrow 2.5 million yuan in cash from our industry. A meeting of member representatives was convened on the 16th of this month to discuss this matter. It was generally agreed that it is difficult to comply with the order given the current commercial depression, and that there is no surplus capacity to cope with the previous loan, which is only a few days away. After repeated discussions, it was decided that it is necessary to exhaust the meager strength because the matter concerns the national treasury and funds are urgently needed for Minister Kong's new appointment. A consensus was reached to raise 1 million yuan, with each bank in the Association borrowing 15,000 yuan. On the 20th of this month, please send the funds directly to the industry reserve, obtain a receipt, and submit it for collection. After the treasury bonds are received, the reserve will distribute them to each bank according to the amount, and return the receipt to clear the procedures. This special notice is hereby recorded and issued, please take note and handle it accordingly. Addressed to ×× Precious Bank, Shanghai Money Trade Association, November 17th, 22nd year.

Yesterday's Payment

According to a Ta Kung Pao reporter's inquiry to the Money Trade Association yesterday, each money shop paid the new loan to the Ministry of Finance to the Joint Reserve of Money Shops yesterday, and obtained a receipt. A total of 67 money shops in the city contributed to the loan, reaching more than 970,000 yuan. The shortfall of just over 20,000 yuan will be covered by the money industry reserve. As for the treasury bonds, they will be received within four or five days after the loan is collected and submitted to the Ministry of Finance. The reserve will then distribute them to each money shop according to the amount.

Electricity Strike Resolved

All Workers Resume Work Tomorrow Morning

Ta Kung Pao reports that the Shanghai electricity strike, which has lasted for two months, has been resolved through the mediation of Mr. Fei Xindun and Du Yuesheng and other Chinese directors. The workers have decided to resume work tomorrow (the 22nd). The details are as follows:

Negotiated Resolution

After Mr. Fei Xindun, Director-General of the Public Works Department, and Mr. Du Yuesheng, a municipal councilor, formally conducted mediation with the company, the two parties reached a general agreement on the resolution method after several consultations. Yesterday, Chinese directors Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Wang Xiaolai, and Lin Kanghou, etc., met again at the Bankers' Association and made a decision. Yesterday morning, Mr. Du and Mr. Yuan conducted final negotiations with the company and reached a resolution: (1) Persuade the workers to resume work first; (2) After the workers resume work, all wages before the strike will be paid in full as before; (3) The company will pay one month's wages for the strike period (if the company refuses to pay the wages, Mr. Du and the Chinese directors will be responsible for the payment). The remaining conditions raised by the workers will be negotiated with the company by Mr. Du and the Chinese directors after the resumption of work. Therefore, the strike has been temporarily resolved.

Resume Work Tomorrow Morning

The 4th District Water and Electricity Industry Union believes that the electricity strike has been resolved through the good-faith mediation of Mr. Fei and Mr. Du. Although the resolution method has not satisfied the workers, they have expressed their willingness to accept it in order to respect the advice of the leaders and to take into consideration the public safety of the area. The union has convened an emergency meeting and decided that the workers of both the old and new factories will resume work tomorrow morning (the 22nd).

Conditions Filed for Record: After the conditions directly resolved by labor and management were signed by the responsible representatives of both parties, the garment union yesterday dispatched representatives Zhang Dongcai and Gao Depei to the Municipal Party Department and the Social Bureau to submit the conditions for record in accordance with labor laws to ensure protection.

Shanghai Police Reporting Station Ordered to be Abolished

After the Shanghai Naval Police Reporting Station was moved to the Coastal Patrol Office, the Ministry of the Navy believed that the police affairs under the jurisdiction of the station could be handled by the two sections of the Patrol Office's navigation police equipment and personnel. It has ordered the original Shanghai Police Reporting Station to be abolished. The director of the station, Chen Zaiheng, and the members of the station, Chen Ruirong and Wang Jiangguang, etc., have all been dismissed and await further appointment. The electrical technicians, signalmen, and service soldiers, etc., are all dismissed and their salaries and public funds are terminated as of November 15. As for the police affairs, the Patrol Office has been ordered to assign personnel from the navigation police equipment and personnel sections to be responsible for handling them in order to save expenses.

Installing New Machines in Pudong

The site of the Pudong Branch of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau is expected to be completed in its entirety within the month. It is scheduled to begin installing 800 door telephone machines at the beginning of next month. The new trunk lines will also be laid according to the routes designated by the Public Works Bureau. It is estimated that there are more than 80 telephones installed in Pudong by the concession telephone company after crossing the boundary. After the Shanghai Telephone Bureau notified the users, more than 40 Bada companies requested to be dismantled and installed in the past few days.

Laying Trans-River Water Lines

Since the formal signing of the temporary contract for the trans-river water line of the Concession Telephone Company directly expanded to Pudong, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau has negotiated with the company to buy it at a price in order to initially recover the sovereignty of the telecommunications administration. It will also set up 75 pairs of trans-river water lines from the Bund of Fuzhou Road to Lan Ni Du in Pudong to connect to the Concession Telephone Company. Fifty pairs of trans-river lines from Gaochang Temple to Zhoujiadu in Pudong will be connected to the Shanghai Telephone Bureau. Both lines are scheduled to be installed starting this morning. The old water line on the Bund of Nanjing Road will be dismantled after the new line is installed and completed.

Adding Round-Trip Lines to Longhua

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau directly connected to Longhua has a total of seven pairs of telephone lines. Because factories, shops, and residences in Xiangjiazhai, Xiaomuqiao, Rihuigang, Fenglinqiao, and other places in Longhua are gradually increasing, the original telephone lines are not enough to allocate. Therefore, 13 additional round-trip lines will be added. Starting from the Telephone Bureau, they will be placed along Lujiabang Road, Manufacturing Bureau Road, Xietu Road, and released to Longhua.

In order to solicit new members for the commercial group, the Municipal Council has appointed Mr. H. E. Arnhold, Mr. P. W. Massey, Mr. C. S. Franklin, and Mr. E. F. Harris at the request of the group commander to form a committee. The committee's recruitment focuses on people of British and American nationality. If necessary, others may be publicly elected to join the committee as members.

Chinese Leprosy Relief Association徵文徵文征文

The Chinese Leprosy Relief Association, in view of the lack of leprosy knowledge among Chinese people, has stipulated that a national leprosy eradication essay contest will be held every two years. It is found that the essay contest was announced and held in October 19 of the Republic of China. The results were quite satisfactory. The second essay contest was also stipulated by the board of directors of the association last month. It is heard that letters and telegrams have been sent from various provinces to request the essay contest rules and purchase reference books. There must be several cases every day, because the essay topic is very common and not limited to specialization. In addition to students above the middle school level, other people from all walks of life are welcome. The deadline for submissions is from now until the end of April next year. All manuscripts submitted by all walks of life have been hired by Dr. Li Ting'an, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, Dr. Zhu Hengbi, Secretary-General of the Chinese Medical Association, and Dr. Pan Guangdan, chief writer of China Youth Weekly, to judge. Cash prizes are also prepared and awarded to the top five winners. The first place is 50 yuan, the second place is 30 yuan, the third place is 15 yuan, the fourth place is 10 yuan, and the fifth place is 5 yuan. For those below the fifth place, a full year of Leprosy Quarterly will be given if the submitted manuscript is selected. All rules and reference books for this essay contest can be inquired by writing to the Chinese Leprosy Relief Association, Nianhao Road, Shanghai Museum.

Robbery of Huge Sum of Money on Huasheng Road, Zhabei

Mr. Zhang, an employee of the Xiexing Minji Military Uniform Factory in Baoqing Lane, Huasheng Road, Zhabei, obtained 6,000 yuan in silver notes from the Xintai Bank at the intersection of Ningbo Road and Jiangxi Road in the Public Concession yesterday morning. He took it back to the military uniform factory's office on Minguo Road, Zhengjia Wood Bridge, and left 1,500 yuan in foreign currency. The remaining 4,500 yuan was taken by Liang Youfang, a factory employee, to Zhabei to distribute part of the wages to female workers. At that time, it was 12:00 noon, and hundreds of female workers were gathered in front of the patio waiting. Liang handed the banknotes to Ma Zhonglian, the accounting room clerk, and Zhang Chungui, an eye clerk, for distribution. Unexpectedly, five robbers suddenly came. Three robbers were wearing blue cloth short shirts and pants, one robber was wearing yellow short clothes, and the other robber was wearing black long clothes. They held guns and guarded the patio entrance, not allowing the workers to go out. The three robbers wearing blue cloth short shirts and pants were also holding pistols, threatening and forbidding them to make noise. A robber in yellow clothes put all the remaining banknotes and silver coins into a lead-skinned iron bucket and left. Before leaving, the robbers re-locked the iron ring on the patio door with lead wire and fled. After checking, 880 yuan of wages had been paid out. The silver notes and coins worth 3,620 yuan were robbed. When the police officers of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau arrived, the robbers had disappeared. Therefore, none of them were captured. However, when the female workers learned that their wages had been robbed, they were afraid that the factory would stop paying their wages, so they gathered and refused to leave. Later, the factory sent someone to the Concession to get some cash and distributed it as usual, and the people's hearts were settled. It is learned that the robbers first destroyed the telephone during the robbery, so it was impossible to report it for a while. The robbers were able to escape the law.

Robbers Break into House and Injure People on Hanzhong Road; One Robber Captured on the Spot

Zhao Guirong, a native of Jiangbei, is 39 years old and lives at No. 7 Dafu Lane, Hanzhong Road, Zhabei. His neighbor is Yin Hengcai, a fellow villager who sells yellow sand and stones for a living. He is diligent and thrifty, so his family has a small amount of assets, which attracted the attention of robbers. At about 6:15 last night, three robbers suddenly used hammers to break through the door and broke into the house. They took out their guns and intimidated them, and searched arbitrarily. The jewelry, clothing, and other items were robbed, the number of which cannot be estimated. After more than ten minutes, the robbers shouted and entered. When the robbers were about to leave, one of the robbers at the back was acting skillfully, but was caught by Zhao Guirong and held down. The robber struggled unsuccessfully, so he fired several shots, hitting Zhao Guirong three times: one shot in the right thigh, one in the left breast, the bullet pierced the left thigh, and one shot remained in the abdomen. Blood was flowing non-stop, and he fainted to the ground. At that time, it was dusk, and neighbors gathered and blew whistles wildly. The police officers nearby immediately arrested a robber on the spot and escorted him to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau for investigation. The injured person was ordered by the police to be rushed to Baolong Hospital for treatment. According to him, Zhao's large intestine had been cut off, and his life was in danger.

Bomb Excavated in Xiaohama, Tanziwan, Injured Four Workers; Feared to be Left Over From Last Year's War; Two Workers in Danger of Death

At around 11:00 yesterday morning, four workers were digging mud in a small river near the wasteland behind the Dafeng Yarn Factory in Tanziwan, Zhabei. Unexpectedly, there was a bomb at the bottom of the river. At that time, the workers did not know what the bomb was. They thought that there might be something hidden in the middle, so they picked up the bomb and placed it on the shore. They used an iron bar to open it. Before the bar had hit it a few times, the bomb was vibrated and suddenly exploded with a loud bang. The pieces of metal flew in all directions. The four workers around the bomb were injured and fell to the ground at the same time. Fortunately, the chief police officers of the Third Division of the Fourth District Police Station heard the sound and rushed to the scene. They immediately notified the Zhabei Fire Brigade to rush to send an ambulance and fly four people to Baolong Hospital on Baker Road for treatment. Pan Ahua, a native of Jiangbei, 19 years old, was injured in the head and limbs, and Liu Changfu, a native of Jiangbei, 35 years old, was injured all over his body and buttocks. It is feared that they are in danger of death. There are also Zhang Daogang, a native of Taizhou, 26 years old, and Xia Yifu, a native of Nanjing, 39 years old, who were injured in both hands and legs, and the situation is still light. After the incident, it was found that the bomb explosion had formed a large hole, and the power of the explosion can be imagined. As for the source of the bomb, it is thought that it was abandoned in the river during the war last year.

Representatives of Western Shipping Merchants in Pudong Request the Municipal Government to Dredge the Shallow Beach in Pudong

Xing Zhigang, a representative of Western shipping merchants in Pudong, submitted a request to the Municipal Government yesterday to dredge the shallow beach along the Pudong south of Dongjiadu Pier in order to facilitate transportation. The document reads: "The petition is to request the dredging of the shallow beach along the Pudong south of Pier 16 in order to maintain shipping and emphasize commercial affairs in the city. Now, the piers along the Pudong are occupied and the river is narrow, resulting in turbulent tides, making driving difficult. Accidents occur from time to time. Recently, the docks have been frequently silted up, and it has been reported to the government for dredging. It is heard that it will only reach Pier 16. Now, from Pier 16 south to Dongjiadu to the area of the South Pier, the Pudong beach is occupied by bamboo rafts and other obstacles, resulting in the accumulation of silt, which is even worse than the pier. Not only can merchant ships not dock, but merchants' goods also have no way to load and unload, which affects commerce and endangers traffic. The importance of ports and road administration is equal. Now, Gongyi Pier, Dongjiadu, and the South Guild Hall Pier are the most popular areas for boats from the four townships to dock and are the commercial center of the southern city. Now that it is planned to dredge to Pier 16, and the shipping pier adjacent to Dongjiadu Pier is close at hand. Both are under the rule of the government, and the shipping merchants are obliged to pay taxes. They should be planned and dredged uniformly. The cost is limited, and success is just around the corner. In order to show our gratitude, we respectfully urge you to approve the order to the Public Works and Public Works Bureaus to plan and dredge as soon as possible in order to maintain shipping and emphasize commercial affairs in the city."

Suddenly, thick smoke filled the air and the fire was blazing. It was extinguished after the fire brigade drove to the scene to put it out. One floor was burned down.

Municipal Party Headquarters Requests Ban on Screening of Anti-War Films

Due to the prevalence of anti-war content in films shown in various cinemas in Shanghai, which has a significant negative impact on our nation's efforts to avenge its grievances and wipe out its humiliation, the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters recently submitted a petition to the Central Party Headquarters, requesting that it consult with the National Government and instruct the Ministry of Interior to prohibit such films. The original text of the petition is excerpted below:

"Petition regarding a request: Upon investigation, many films shown in cinemas in this city contain anti-war themes. For example, the recently released 'War and Peace' depicts the cruelty of war, the sorrow of families being torn apart, the suffering of wounded soldiers, the aimless existence of officers after the war, the sadness and pity of disabled veterans, and the desolate and tragic scenes of soldiers' graves, etc., which are enough to make viewers feel chilled and frightened. Although its intention may be to call for peace, in this time of serious national crisis for the Chinese nation, if the public's thoughts are immersed in such images, then the vow to 'endure hardship and avenge national humiliation' will become mere after-dinner banter. The impact on the nation's destiny will be profound and immense. This committee, considering the difficulties of the times, cannot bear to remain silent and therefore submits this document to your esteemed council. We respectfully request your council to review and approve this matter, consult with the National Government, and order the Ministry of Interior to prohibit the screening of such films within the country, and instruct the Film Censorship Committee to pay strict attention. This is for the public good."

Chinese Woman Traveling to Japan Expelled by Japanese Police and Returned to Shanghai

A man named Wu Caogen from Yangjing Town, Pudong, was invited to work at the Eiki Gofukuten Kimono Shop in Kawaramachi, Kyoto, Japan. When he departed from Shanghai, he brought a woman named Wu (23 years old) with him to Japan, intending for her to work as a maid in a Chinese merchant's house in Yokohama. They had already boarded a ship to Japan. However, when the ship arrived in Kobe, Wu Caogen was detained by the Japanese water police and not allowed to enter the country. Despite Wu's statement that he had an employer, it was to no avail. The woman Wu, who went with him, was also prohibited from landing in Yokohama. Later, when the Chinese merchant who hired her arrived to vouch for her, the Japanese police still refused to allow it. Consequently, Ms. Wu and Wu Caogen, along with three other Chinese people, Mr. Weng, Mr. Zhu, etc., were all detained at the police station and escorted back to Shanghai yesterday on the Asosan Maru. This is the first instance of Japanese people rejecting Chinese women from entering the country and even insulting them. Yesterday, Ms. Wu and the others arrived in Shanghai and have already returned to their hometown of Yangjing Town.

Haikyong Performer's Circus to Perform Today for Charity to Help Disaster Victims - Closing at the End of the Month to Prepare for Departure to India

Today, the Haikyong Performer's Circus will hold two shows, both day and night, and all proceeds from ticket sales will be donated to the Flood Relief Committee to assist the victims of the Yellow River flood. As this performance is charitable in nature, a large crowd is expected. Mr. Shi Huid, the circus's general manager, reported that the daytime show will begin at 2:30 PM, and the nighttime show will begin at 9:15 PM. Each show will feature the usual 20 acts. The Haikyong Performer's Circus is always willing to lend a hand to charitable causes during its world tours. Therefore, when the members of the Flood Relief Committee contacted them, the circus immediately agreed, resulting in a very satisfactory outcome.

The circus will leave Shanghai for India in two weeks. Those who have not yet seen it or wish to see it again should go as soon as possible to feast their eyes. The circus will stop performing at the end of this month to prepare for its trip. It is said that the recent performances have been the most spectacular ever seen, and the menagerie contains many rare and exotic animals. To date, over ten thousand people have visited. One more thing to inform the audience is that the circus will light many large stoves before the show to make the air inside the tent warmer. These stoves will be removed before the curtain rises.

The Shanghai Charity Organizations United Relief Association for the Yellow River Flood, consisting of Xu Shiying, Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, etc., requested the Haikyong Performer's Circus to perform a charity show today (the 21st). All proceeds from the day's ticket sales, after deducting the circus's expenses of 5,000 yuan and advertising costs, as well as a 1,000 yuan gift to the circus, will be donated to the Yellow River Flood Relief Association. Mr. Xu Shiying delivered a speech of thanks, saying: "This year, the Yellow River has flooded, the levees have breached, and the provinces along the river have suffered severe flooding. The most heavily affected areas cover approximately 15,600 square li, and the number of affected people is approximately 2.9 million. Currently, the disaster victims in various places are without clothes, food, or shelter, crying out for help, truly a hell on earth. Our association is handling emergency relief for Shandong, Henan, and Hebei provinces, and it is a critical time. Today, Mr. Haikyong, the German circus performer, with a spirit of universal love, is helping disaster victims and caring for neighbors, and has put on special new performances to raise funds for relief. We are also grateful to the Chinese and foreign gentlemen and ladies who have come to watch and are enthusiastic about the relief effort. I am immensely grateful. On behalf of the members of this association and the disaster-stricken compatriots, I express my thanks and will broadcast a thank you message on the Greater China Radio Station tomorrow."

The Suspected Mastermind of the Murder of the "Taiji King" in Nanchang Apprehended in Shanghai - A Letter from Wu Zuyin Discovered During Inspection of Postal and Telegraph Services - Deemed Highly Suspicious and Personnel Sent to Shanghai to Arrest Him - Complex Inside Story, Motivated by Adultery

Nanchang, the capital of Jiangxi Province, has a well-known lewd woman named Zhang Tan, who specializes in seducing the daughters of prominent families and the wives and concubines of wealthy gentry in the local area to secretly engage in prostitution. The people of Nanchang have bestowed upon her the lofty title of "Taiji King." Those who frequent her house for pleasure are all military and political figures, prominent gentry, and wealthy merchants. Therefore, the Taiji King's power is immense, and people on the streets are wary of her. Local officials are well aware that she is the ringleader in corrupting public morals, but due to various concerns, they are unwilling to bring her to justice, which has only made the Taiji King more reckless. On the night of the 10th of this month, several members of a certain "Exterminate the Traitor" group suddenly rushed into the Taiji King's residence at No. 10 Baojia Lane. At that time, several young women who had been seduced were enjoying themselves with their patrons, while the Taiji King was alone in the Buddhist hall,

Chanting Sutras and Tapping a Wooden Fish

When reciting the Buddhist scriptures, the group members immediately divided into groups to work. They locked the shameless men and women in a room, cut the electrical wires in the house, and removed the light bulbs. Then, in the darkness, they stabbed Zhang Tan, the notorious troublemaker who shook Jiangxi, to death in front of the Buddhist altar. Before leaving, the murderers left behind numerous printed materials, including a letter to the people of Jiangxi and a list of Zhang Tan's crimes with prominent red seals inside the house. Later, the maid of the house, after the group had left for a long time, dared to come out to get a light and illuminate the house. This tragic scene was then exposed, and she immediately reported it to the local Public Security Bureau, which dispatched police to investigate and found a sharp blade beside the corpse. The next day, it was reported to the local court, which appointed a prosecutor to the scene to examine the body and order its burial. The highest military and police authorities in the area believed that such an assassination case had occurred in the capital of the province, and that the perpetrators dared to issue a declaration afterward, showing extreme disregard for the law. In addition to ordering a thorough investigation of the murderers, they also ordered the postal and telegraph offices to implement postal and telegraph inspections from that day onward. As a result of the inspection, a letter from Wu Zuyin of Jiangxi to a certain father-in-law, Mr. Qi, in Shanghai was discovered,

Deemed Highly Suspicious of the Tragedy

Therefore, Zhang Shouchun, the director of the Public Security Branch, was dispatched to Shanghai to track him down. After learning that Wu was residing at Room 226, Yangtze Hotel, Yunnan Road, Director Zhang went to the Zhabei Police Station the night before last at 9:30 PM and requested that Detective He Lianzhen be dispatched to the address to arrest Wu. It was found that Wu was one of the wealthy gentry of Nanchang and had a family there. In the past, Wu was also a guest in Zhang Tan's "Taiji" inner circle. Later, through her introduction, he met a woman named Qi Yiqing, the daughter of Mr. Qi. Initially, they only had a fleeting relationship, but later, due to their mutual affection, he took her as a concubine and hid her in No. 4 Hedemiao. Yiqing is now only in her early twenties. After becoming Wu's concubine, she still could not forget the "Taiji" lifestyle. In addition, Zhang Tan was good at seduction, so she often secretly went to Baojia Lane behind Wu's back to

Try the Flavor of Extramarital Affairs

Over time, the matter was heard by Wu. He was reluctant to abandon her, so he sent Yiqing to her parents' house at No. 31 Fulu Nunnery, so that she would be far away from the den of iniquity and could be disciplined by her parents, hoping she would wake up. However, Yiqing was fickle by nature and could not change her ways after all. Wu then moved her to a silver shop on Zhongshan Road, but the red apricot still climbed over the wall, and he was destined to wear the green hat forever. Wu could not help but resent the Taiji King and wanted to recruit warriors to kill her to eliminate the potential troubles at home. He learned of Wang Gao, who was a vagrant. He conspired with him and promised a large sum of money if he succeeded. Wang readily agreed. However, Wang had committed a serious crime during the warlord era and was arrested by the authorities, sentenced to death, and imprisoned awaiting execution. Between 1926 and 1927, the warlord regime collapsed, and the situation in Jiangxi changed. Zhang Tan's prominence was rising, and Wang was pardoned and released with her help. He was grateful for the life-saving grace, but had no time to repay her.

He was Willing to Put Her to Death

Therefore, after Wu asked him, he told her about it. Li Shanji, the most reputable lawyer in Nanchang, also frequented the "Taiji" on weekdays and had a close relationship with Zhang Tan. Zhang Tan once relayed what Wang had said to Li and asked for advice on preventive measures. Li replied that it was impossible to verify whether Wang's words were credible or whether Wu actually had such a plan, and advised the Taiji King to be tolerant or even avoid him. Therefore, although the Taiji King and Wu each had their own pain, they never openly confronted each other. It was Lawyer Li's words that resolved the dispute. Recently, the Taiji King received various anonymous letters, all with threatening words, and was very worried. Two days before she was killed, she even

Consulted a Fortune Teller About Good and Bad Omens

According to the fortune teller, she was about to have an unexpected disaster and should protect herself quickly. Therefore, she planned to relocate to avoid it, but she was just starting to arrange the move when it was too late. After the incident, the military law department of the headquarters investigated the matter and summoned Wang Gao. Under interrogation, it was confirmed that Wu was indeed a suspect. Coincidentally, a letter from Wu sent from Shanghai was discovered, so Director Zhang was immediately dispatched to Shanghai to arrest him. As for Wu, he left Jiangxi three days (the 7th) before the tragedy occurred, took a plane to Shanghai on the 8th, and first stayed at Room 614, Nanjing Hotel, under the alias Liu Zilin. On the 9th, he moved to Yipinxiang, first staying in Room 61, and then switching to Room 62 on the 10th. It wasn't until the 11th that he

Arrived at the Yangtze Hotel

He opened Room 401, stayed for three nights, and then switched to Room 229. His movements were extremely suspicious. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Court, where Judge Qian interrogated him. Police Lawyer Zhang Shizhu explained the details of the arrest. Because Nanchang requested extradition, he should provide concrete evidence. Wu hired Lawyer Jiang Yiping to apply for bail. Judge Qian questioned Wu, who flatly denied murdering Zhang Tan. The court stated that the case still needed to be investigated and ordered Wu to be detained for a seven-day extension for further interrogation.

Business Offices on Both Routes Began Handling Delivery of Goods Yesterday - Liable for Compensation in Case of Damage or Loss - Six Classes of Charges, Must Be Fully Packaged

The business office of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways has been successively launching services such as answering inquiries, handling luggage, handling packages, booking hotels, booking sleepers, and selling passenger tickets. The most important business of handling goods delivery, after much preparation by the office, is now ready and has been approved by the Transportation Department. It began operating yesterday, and the details are as follows:

Dispatch (1) For merchants who have goods to dispatch, they only need to notify the office by telephone, and the office will immediately dispatch a car to pick up the goods at the station, handle all dispatch procedures, and then send the bill of lading to the merchant's office to collect the freight. (2) For goods arriving in Shanghai, merchants can also entrust the office to pick them up from the warehouse and send them to the designated location. (3) Merchants who have their own trucks for transporting goods do not need the office to pick them up, but can still have the office handle the procedures. Furthermore, for the convenience of merchants, the office has set up a "Freight Contact Office" at the old inquiry office at the North Station to facilitate all parties to contact everything at any time.

Receipt of Goods (A) Receipt of Goods (1) Merchants who have goods that need to be transported by freight train from Shanghai to other locations can entrust the office to pick them up at the station in accordance with the provisions of this method and handle all dispatch procedures. (2) Goods entrusted to the office for pick-up and declaration must be completely packaged or tightly sealed, and the names and addresses of the consignor and consignee must be clearly marked for dispatch and delivery. (3) The office charges for picking up goods on behalf of customers are as follows: First and second class goods, 3 jiao per 100 kilograms; third and fourth class goods, 2.5 jiao per 100 kilograms; fifth and sixth class goods, 2 jiao per 100 kilograms. For each batch of goods, if the total weight is less than 500 kilograms, it will be calculated as 500 kilograms. If it is more than 500 kilograms and less than 1,000 kilograms, it will be calculated as 1,000 kilograms. (4) When the office dispatches a vehicle to pick up goods, the office's accompanying cargo clerk will jointly inspect the goods with the consignor and issue a receipt for the picked-up goods on the spot for the exchange of the bill of lading. (5) When picking up goods, the consignor shall sign and seal the consignment note to clarify responsibility. (6) After the goods are declared and loaded, the office will immediately send the goods receipt or delivery order to the consignor, and at the same time collect the advance freight, loading and unloading costs, and the office's pick-up fee, and return the receipt for the picked-up goods to the office to clear the procedures. (7) The office has receipts for goods pick-up and delivery fees, which are given to the customer for safekeeping. The consignor shall pay based on this receipt each time the pick-up fee is paid. (8) If the entrusted goods are deemed to have suspicious content or are unsuitable for transportation, the office's accompanying cargo clerk may refuse to accept them or request an on-site inspection. (9) If there is damage or loss due to the office's negligence, it will be handled in accordance with the General Rules for the Responsible Transportation of Railway Freight Cars of the Republic of China. (10) The office will temporarily not accept the following goods: 1. Bulky vehicles such as sedans, boats, airplanes, etc.; 2. Live poultry and livestock; 3. Explosive or dangerous goods. (11) Customers who entrust the office to handle dispatch procedures but do not pick up the goods can also have them handled, but each item must be charged a handling fee of 5 cents, with a minimum of 5 jiao per batch. (B) Delivery of Goods (1) For merchants who have goods that have arrived in Shanghai via the railway's freight train, they can entrust the office to pick them up and deliver them in accordance with the provisions of this method. (2) Consignees who wish to entrust the office to pick up and deliver goods must submit the freight receipt or delivery order, pay all freight and miscellaneous fees paid upon arrival, and the office's delivery fee, and exchange them for the office's receipt for entrusted goods before delivery can be arranged. (3) The office charges the same for delivering goods on behalf of customers as for picking up goods. (4) The office has receipts for goods pick-up and delivery fees, which are given to the customer for safekeeping. The consignee shall pay based on this receipt each time the delivery fee is paid. (5) When the goods are delivered, the consignee shall return the office's receipt for entrusted goods to the office's accompanying cargo clerk to clear the procedures. (6) If the entrusted goods are lost due to the office's negligence, it will be handled in accordance with the General Rules for the Responsible Transportation of Freight Matters. (7) If the arriving goods are found to be damaged, the office may postpone delivery and notify the consignee to inspect them at the station for processing. (8) Customers who entrust the office to pick up goods (but not deliver them) or handle requests for compensation can also have them handled, but each item must be charged a handling fee of 5 cents, with a minimum of 5 jiao per batch.

The National Goods Association Introduces Yingfeng Embroidery Thread

The Shanghai Citizens' Association for the Promotion of National Goods deeply laments that the embroidery thread and cross-stitch cloth used by various girls' schools and boudoir ladies are all foreign products, with profits flowing overseas, amounting to more than 2 million yuan annually. After investigation, it has been found that the Golden Hand brand embroidery thread and cross-stitch thread produced by the factory member Rongfeng Embroidery Thread Factory are excellent and superior to foreign goods. Yesterday, special letters were sent to all large and medium-sized girls' schools and well-known embroiderers in Shanghai, requesting them to lead the promotion in order to protect national goods. The original letter is recorded below: (abridged above) According to the letter from our association member Rongfeng Embroidery Thread Factory, the member's Golden Hand trademark various-colored cross-stitch thread is a necessity for embroidery and sewing, with soft and excellent material and bright and non-fading colors. The manufacturing is deeply researched and superior to foreign products. However, because the product is newly launched, publicity is not widespread. Please promote and introduce it to encourage the female community to try it, etc., to the association. After investigation, the products of the factory are one of the emerging crafts of national goods. They have been reviewed by our association and are beautiful and superior to foreign goods. We have always admired your school's enthusiasm for national goods and exquisite embroidery. Therefore, in accordance with the provisions of Article 6, Paragraph 1 of Chapter 2 of the association's articles of association, we are responsible for the introduction. We sincerely hope that you will quickly promote it, test the medicine, and maintain national goods and recover profits. Mr. Hu Zhenjia, the manager of the factory, is carrying samples and is moving forward to present them. Please contact him for details (abridged below). It is also learned that the factory has submitted 50,000 skeins of various colored samples and 10,000 copies of finely printed embroidery samples to expand publicity and promote trust, to be given to the female community for trial use.

A Record of the Scientific Instrument Museum's Reception for Sponsors

The Scientific Instrument Museum on Qipan Street in Shanghai recently expanded its business and increased its capital in response to the needs of the times. A welcome reception for sponsors was held on the 19th at noon in the main hall of Yipinxiang. More than 30 people from political, business, educational and other circles, including Wu Tiecheng, Pan Gongzhan, Zhan Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Zhuang Songfu, and Wang Yansong, attended, creating a lively atmosphere. Mr. Gu Dingmei, the director of the museum, presided over the meeting and delivered a welcome speech. Next, General Manager Zhou Jingting gave an overview of the museum's history of promoting science for more than 30 years and its future expansion plans. Then, Mr. Zhang Yuanruo, representing Mayor Wu, gave a speech, saying that if you want to do a good job, you must first sharpen your tools, and instruments are the tools for scientific research, etc., elaborating on this point in detail. Education Director Pan said that to promote science, we should first eliminate the traditional mysterious concept of science. The museum can work hard to improve manufacturing, reduce costs, and popularize science. Not only should there be cheap, beautiful, and applicable scientific instruments to supply schools, but it is also important for the public to have the opportunity to come into contact with them at any time, and he expressed his sympathy, etc. Others, such as Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Zhuang Songfu, Zhang Naiqi, and Guan Baiyi, also believed that science is the mother of improving all undertakings. Recently, the call for scientific nation and scientific management has become increasingly louder. To promote science, we must first develop the instrument industry. Therefore, the expansion of the Scientific Instrument Museum this time is also something that today's patriots should work together to achieve, etc. Finally, Mr. Lin Dian, the director of the museum, gave a thank-you speech. The guests and hosts parted in a pleasant atmosphere.

Standard Brand Light Bulb Trademark Approved for Registration

The Standard Brand light bulb produced by the Shanghai Light Bulb Company, with a circular trademark drawn in both Chinese and English, was submitted to the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry for registration. After the Trademark Bureau's review and approval, and after a considerable period of time, with no objections, and with no violations of the Trademark Law, the bureau approved the registration and issued a registration certificate. In the future, if any competitor imitates or counterfeits the company's above trademark, the company will pursue legal action.

Verdict in the Lawsuit of Two Dancers - Gao Lili Fined 30 Yuan

Yin Qiulian, a dancer at the Anle Palace, sued her colleague Gao Lili for assault and filed a civil suit to recover damages. At the trial, the plaintiff's careless remarks caused a nationality issue, almost leading to a major uproar. After a retrial, the plaintiff solemnly stated that her place of origin was Shenyang, Liaoning Province, which completely eliminated the previous misunderstanding. The alleged assault was also clearly investigated. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui of the First Special District Court announced the verdict, but both the plaintiff and the defendant failed to appear as scheduled. The main text of the judgment stated that the defendant was guilty of assault and was fined 30 yuan. If unable to pay, she will be allowed to commute to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The civil suit portion will be transferred to the civil court for handling.

Forged Circus Tickets Case Heard Yesterday - Printing Shop Owner and Partner Transferred to Special Court

Li Zhongyun and Wang Guangrong, ticket sellers at the Haikyong Performer's Circus, colluded with Ren Linxiang, a postman from Post Office No. 618, to forge the circus's one-yuan and two-yuan admission tickets at the Fuxing Printing Shop at No. 1303 Zhonghua Road in the Nanshi District, for the purpose of selling them and profiting. After the case was discovered, Hua Detective Wang Yongjun and Zhu Shanghe of the Jing'an Temple Police Station first detained Li, Wang, and Ren and sent them to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. At the same time, they went to the Fuxing Printing Shop in the Nanshi District and arrested the owner, Ms. Li Liu, and the shop partner, Yao Jiqing. Two printing plates, two packages of type, and 220 forged tickets were seized and sent to the Public Security Bureau for questioning. This matter has already been reported in this newspaper. Now, the Special Court has prepared an official document and sent it to the police station. Detective Wang and others went to the Public Security Bureau the day before yesterday and took Ms. Li and Yao, along with the seized items, and transferred them to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were transferred to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Special Court. According to Police Lawyer Wang Yaotang, the defendant, Ms. Li Liu, is the owner of the Fuxing Printing Shop in the Nanshi District, and Yao is the partner. They colluded with the already arrested Li Zhongyun and others to forge circus tickets worth 1,498 yuan, violating Article 224 of the Criminal Law regarding the crime of forgery of documents. Therefore, they are being prosecuted. However, Li Zhongyun's case is scheduled to be heard on the 22nd of this month. Therefore, a request is made to allow the cases to be tried together. After Judge Wu Tingqi briefly questioned Ms. Li and Yao, he ordered them to be detained separately and await a rescheduled hearing with Li Zhongyun on Wednesday of this week.

A Young Woman Sacrifices Herself at a Flower Gambling Session - Chen Suzhen Hangs Herself in Despair

Jiang Songshan, 39 years old, a native of Jiangdu, is a partner at the Nianhe Seafood Store on Xinkaihe Road in the Chinese Concession of Nanshi. He lives at No. 6 Jinshan Lane, Anping Street, inside the old North Gate. He married a woman surnamed Chen from his hometown in his early years. She is now 36 years old and has a daughter named Guiying, who is 14 years old. Unexpectedly, in the spring of this year, Jiang suddenly became acquainted with a woman named Chen Suzhen from Suzhou. Unexpectedly, Suzhen had a gambling addiction, especially for flower gambling. As a result, all of her clothes and jewelry were pawned. Although Jiang hated it, because Suzhen was already pregnant, he had no choice but to move Suzhen to Jinshan Lane to live with his legal wife, hoping that someone would watch over her. However, yesterday morning around 2:00 AM, while Jiang and his legal wife were sound asleep, they suddenly heard a loud noise in Suzhen's bedroom. Knowing that something was wrong, they quickly put on their clothes and checked, only to see that Suzhen had hanged herself. Although they tried to take her down, it was too late, and she was beyond saving. They immediately reported it to the Second Precinct of the First District and ordered the neighborhood head to report it to the local court for examination.

Zhong Yunliang Mistakenly Beaten and Killed - Body Examined

Zhong Yunliang, 32 years old, from Suzhou, resided at No. 94 Yongchang Lane, Dongyouheng Road. He worked at the Dingfeng Silk Factory on Xiangyanqiao Road in Zhabei. Around 10:00 PM on the 17th of this month, Zhong and his companion, Shen Xingsen, finished work at the factory and were returning home. Unexpectedly, as soon as they walked out of the factory gate together, several men were waiting there, holding iron bars, intending to beat Shen. Seeing this, Zhong immediately stepped forward to dissuade them, and was severely beaten in the abdomen. Shen, seeing that things were not good, immediately hid and avoided the disaster. Zhong returned home with injuries, and the wound became increasingly painful. Later, his roommate, Xu Fenggang, took him to Tongren Hospital, but the treatment was ineffective, and he died soon after. The hospital reported it to the Hongkou Police Station, which ordered Detective Yang Xichen to investigate. It was learned that the number of men who committed the crime had previously worked at the Dingfeng Silk Factory, but for some reason, they were suddenly laid off by the factory. They suspected that Shen was responsible, leading to a feud. Therefore, they ambushed there that night, intending to retaliate. Unexpectedly, they mistakenly beat Zhong. The detective then carried the body to the Philan Road Morgue. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei of the First Special District Court came to the morgue to examine the body. After examining the body, he learned from Shen Xingsen that the deceased Zhong Yunliang, male, had indeed died from an abdominal injury sustained during his life. The body was handed over to Shen Xingsen, who signed a guarantee to take it back for burial. It is now known that the incident occurred in the Chinese Concession, and the responsible Public Security Bureau is currently engaged in arresting the perpetrators.

Dong Zhixin Accused of Selling Counterfeit Goods, Fined 300 Yuan by Court

Dong Zhixin, the unscrupulous owner of Dexingxiang Department Store at No. 5, Lane 1, Yela Street, French Concession, has recently been selling inferior goods. The triangular-branded women's gloves he sells have trademarks and patterns identical to the Baoshi brand gloves registered by the Zhongnan Factory at No. 228, Ladu Road. The Zhongnan Factory discovered this and accused Dong of profiting from trademark infringement, which hinders the promotion of domestic goods and is intolerable. Therefore, they immediately reported it to the police. Detectives were dispatched to Dexingxiang, where a dozen pairs of counterfeit gloves and a ledger of alteration fees were seized, and Dong was arrested and brought to the Second Special District Court. He was publicly prosecuted for harming agriculture, industry, and commerce. Yesterday, Judge Qiu Huan-ying of the Eighth Criminal Court ruled that Dong Zhixin knowingly sold goods with counterfeit trademarks and fined him 300 yuan. If he fails to pay the fine, he will be imprisoned at a rate of 2 yuan per day. Before the judgment is finalized, the number of days of detention will be used to offset the fine at a rate of 2 yuan per day.
